03/11/2019, 20:18 - Saras: Now discussing about the shortcomings
1.A single drone will be incapable to monitor multiple areas of crop simultaneously,so inspecting the entire area at single instance of time is not possible. However this problem can be solved by using multiple drones for lager fields.
2.Drone tech is not so common yet and requires skills for operation. Technicians are required to interact with the softwares which could be really costly. Drones , hardware, software and tech ,all combined will be a huge investment to be made for a small scaled farmer.
3.The agricultural drones are weather dependent and require critical attention towards maintenance . although drones are water,dust resistant but they are not yet well compatible to withstand stormy conditions. Which might be disappointing to farmers. However we might expect better performance in future
4.There are certain guidelines one has to follow in order to fly drones. I.e. register to DGCA,getting UID,ADC. Flight plans must be reported to the nearest airports which may render the drone flight due to air schedule. Hence air space traffic might cause some problems yo drone flight
 

Coming to a conclusion, however drone technology has some limitations but these are not that couldnâ€™t be solved. With development , the drones will prove to be the most important and reliable tool to the farmers in future. Increasing population is leading to inc in demand of food production 
making farming industry grow in future which makes agricultural drone industry worth investing in

03/11/2019, 20:38 - Tanisha: Drone use in agriculture is growing as more farmers realise the technology's ability to perform key tasks and its fast developing potential to take on bigger roles in the future.
The drone helps in farming Â in order to increaseÂ crop production and monitor crop growth.
Sensors and digital imaging capabilities gives farmers a richer picture of their fields. This information proves useful in improving crop yields and farm efficiency. The drone can survey the crops for the farmer periodically to their liking. Weekly, daily, or even hourly, pictures can show the changes in the crops over time, thus showing possible â€œtrouble spotsâ€.Â 
The affordability of the drone and rapid advances in the scope of the technology are fuelling an ever widening range of current uses. 
These include aerial mapping,  plant health monitoring, weed detection, water sprinkling and crop spraying. Additional uses include keeping track of livestock, surveying fences, and monitoring for plant pathogens.
According to a new report, the worldwideÂ Agriculture Drones marketÂ is anticipated to reach around USD 8,019.8 million by 2026. North America is expected to be the leading contributor to the globalÂ marketÂ in 2017.

{
	int value,pos,n=1;
		while(n)
	{

	scanf("%d",&value);
	printf("enter the  position");

		{
			printf("pos not found");

		}

	temp=temp->next;

CURSOR C1 IS SELECT * FROM EMP ORDER BY SAL DESC ;
REC C1 % ROWTYPE;
BEGIN 
OPEN C1;
LOOP 
FETCH C1 INTO REC;

DBMS_OUTPUT.PUT_LINE('EMP NO:'||REC.E_NO||'   EMP NAME:'||REC.E_NAME||' JOB:'||REC.JOB||' SALARY:'||REC.SAL);
END LOOP;
CLOSE C1;
END;

T NUMBER;

BEGIN 
FOR REC IN C1(4) LOOP

EXIT WHEN C1%NOTFOUND;
END LOOP;
END;

04/05/2020, 20:07 - Saras: CREATE TABLE EMP(E_NO NUMBER(10) PRIMARY KEY,E_NAME CHAR(30),JOB CHAR(20),SAL NUMBER(10));
CREATE OR REPLACE PROCEDURE INSERT_EMP(E_NO IN NUMBER,E_NAME IN CHAR,JOB IN CHAR,SAL IN NUMBER) IS
BEGIN
INSERT INTO EMP VALUES(E_NO,E_NAME,JOB,SAL);
END;
DECLARE
NO NUMBER;
SALARY NUMBER;
EJOB CHAR(10);
NAME CHAR(10);
BEGIN
NO:=1;
NAME:='SARAS';
EJOB:='XYZ';
SALARY:=100000;
INSERT_EMP(NO,NAME,EJOB,SALARY);
END;

06/05/2020, 13:10 - Tanisha: Modifying and Interfering Inputs
In some cases, the sensor output will be influenced by physical variables other than the intended
measurand. In Figure 1.4, X is the intended measurand, Y is an interfering input, and Z is a modifying
input. The interfering input Y causes the sensor to respond in the same manner as the linear superposition
of Y and the intended measurand X. The measured signal output is therefore a combination of X and Y, with Y interfering with the intended measurand X. An example of an interfering input would be a
structural vibration within a force measurement system.
Modifying inputs changes the behavior of the sensor or measurement system, thereby modifying the
input/output relationship and calibration of the device. This is shown schematically in Figure 1.5. For
various values of Z in Figure 1.5, the slope of the calibration curve changes. Consequently, changing Z
will result in a change of the apparent measurement even if the physical input variable X remains constant.
A common example of a modifying input is temperature; it is for this reason that many devices are
calibrated at specified temperatures.

21/05/2020, 19:36 - Saras: #include <iostream>
using namespace std;
void countingsort(int A1[],int n,int exp)
{
    int i,A3[n+1],A2[10]={0};
    for(i=0;i<n;i++)
    {
    A2[A1[i]/exp%10]++;
    }
    for(i=1;i<n;i++)
    {
        A2[i]=A2[i]+A2[i-1];
    }
    for(i=0;i<n;i++)
    {
        A3[(n+1)-A2[(A1[i]/exp)%10]]=A1[i];
        A2[(A1[i]/exp)%10]--;
    }
    for(i=0;i<n;i++)
    {
        A1[i]=A3[i+1];
    }
    for(i=0;i<n;i++)
    {
        cout<<A1[i]<<" ";
    }
}
    void radixsort(int A1[],int k,int n)
    {
        for(int exp=1;k/exp>0;exp*=10)
        {
        countingsort(A1,n,exp);
        }
    }

int main()
{
    int n,i,k=0;
    cin>>n;
    int A1[n];
    for( i=0;i<n;i++)
    {
        cin>>A1[i];
    }
    for(i=0;i<n;i++)
    {
        if (A1[i]>k)
        {
            k=A1[i];
        }
    }
    radixsort(A1,k,n);
    cout<<"\n"
    for(i=0;i<n;i++)
    {
        cout<<A1[i]<<" ";
    }
	return 0;
}

21/05/2020, 19:39 - Tanisha: #include <iostream>
using namespace std;
int getMax(int arr[], int n)
{
	int max=arr[0];
	for (int i = 1; i < n; i++)
	if (arr[i] > max)
	max=arr[i];
	return max;
}
void countSort(int arr[],int n,int exp)
{int op[n];int  count[10] = {0};
	for (int i = 0; i < n; i++)
	count[9-(arr[i]/exp)%10]++;
	for (int i = 1; i < 10; i++)
	count[i] += count[i-1];
	for (int i = n - 1; i >= 0; i--)
	{
		op[count[9-(arr[i]/exp)%10]-1]=arr[i];
		count[9-(arr[i]/exp)%10]--;
	}
	for (int i = 0; i < n; i++)
		arr[i] = op[i];
}
void radixsort(int arr[], int n)
{
	int m = getMax(arr, n);
	for (int exp=1;m/exp>0;exp *= 10)
    {
        countSort(arr,n,exp);
        for (int i = 0; i < n; i++)
		cout<<arr[i]<<" ";
        cout<<endl;
}}
 
int main()
{
int n;
cin>>n;
int arr[n];
for(int i = 0; i < n; i++)
cin>>arr[i];
radixsort(arr,n);
return 0;
}

18/08/2020, 15:08 - Saras: gs = [[2,8,1],[0,4,3],[7,6,5]]
a = [[1,2,3], [8, 0, 4], [7,6,5]]
print(gs)
def left(x,y):
    temp=a[x][y-1]
    a[x][y-1]=a[x][y]
    a[x][y]=temp
def right(x,y):
    temp=a[x][y+1]
    a[x][y+1]=a[x][y]
    a[x][y]=temp
def up(x,y):
    temp=a[x-1][y]
    a[x-1][y]=a[x][y]
    a[x][y]=temp
def down(x,y):
    temp=a[x+1][y]
    a[x+1][y]=a[x][y]
    a[x][y]=temp
up(1,1)
print(a)
print(gs)
left(0,1)
print(a)
print(gs)
down(0,0)
print(a)
print(gs)
right(1,0)
print(a)
print(gs)
right(1,1)
print(a)
print(gs)
up(1,2)
print(a)
print(gs)
left(0,2)
print(a)
print(gs)
left(0,1)
print(a)
print(gs)
down(0,0)
print(a)
print(gs)

 l1.append(random.randint(100,900))

odd=[]
even=[]
prime=[]
codd=0
ceven=0
cp=0
for n in l1:
    if(n%2==0):
        ceven += 1
        even.append(n)
    else:
        codd += 1
        odd.append(n)
    for i in range(2, n):
        if (n % i) == 0:
            break
    else:
        cp += 1
        prime.append(n)

print(str(codd)+str(" odd: ")+str(odd))
print(str(ceven)+str(" even: ")+str(even))
print(str(cp)+str(" prime: ")+str(prime))

17/11/2020, 20:11 - Saras: #include<iostream>
#include<math.h>
using namespace std;
int count=0;
void disp(int a[], int n)
{
//print array
/*for(int i=0;i<n;i++)
{
cout<<a[i];
cout<<endl;
}
 print pattern*/
for(int i=0;i<n;i++)
{
	for (int j=0;j<n;j++)
{
if(j!=a[i])
cout<<"0\t";
else
cout<<"1\t";
}
cout<<endl;
}

}

int issafe(int result[],int x2,int y2)
{
for(int i=0;i<x2;i++)
{
if(result[i]==y2||abs(i-x2)==abs(result[i]-y2))
return 0;
}
return 1;
}
void placement(int result[], int x, int size)
{
for(int i=0;i<size;i++)
{
if(issafe(result,x,i)==1)
	{
	result[x]=i;
	if(size-1==x)
	{
	cout<<"Solution found\n";
	count++;
	disp(result,size);
	}
	placement(result,x+1,size);
	}
}
}

int main()
{
int result[100],n;
cout<<"enter board size";
cin>>n;
result[n];
placement(result,0,n);
cout<<"\nNo. of solns"<<count;
return 0;
}

#include<iostream>
using namespace std;


bool canPlace(char board[][100],int row,int col,int n){

    ///Row mein queen to nahi h
    for(int i=0;i<n;i++){
        if(board[row][i]=='Q'){
            return false;
        }
    }
    ///Col mein queen to nahi h
    for(int i=0;i<n;i++){
        if(board[i][col]=='Q'){
            return false;
        }
    }
    /// Diagonals
    ///Top Left
    int i=row,j=col;
    while(i>=0&&j>=0){
        if(board[i][j]=='Q'){
            return false;
        }
        i--;
        j--;
    }
    ///Top Right
    i=row,j=col;
    while(i>=0 && j<n){
        if(board[i][j]=='Q'){
            return false;
        }
        i--;
        j++;
    }

    return true;
}



bool solveNQueen(char board[][100],int n,int row){
    if(row==n){
        ///Print the board
        for(int x=0;x<n;x++){
            for(int y=0;y<n;y++){
                cout<<board[x][y]<<" ";
            }
            cout<<endl;

        }

        return true;
    }

    ///Rec Case

    ///Try to place the queen in the current row

    for(int pos=0;pos<n;pos++){

            if(canPlace(board,row,pos,n)){
                    board[row][pos]='Q';

                    bool agliQueenRakhPayeKya = solveNQueen(board,n,row+1);
                    if(agliQueenRakhPayeKya==true){
                        return true;
                    }

                    board[row][pos]='.';
            }

    }
    ///Backtracking
    return false;
}

return 0;

17/11/2020, 20:11 - Saras: #include<iostream>
 using namespace std;
 int mcm(int dim[],int n)
 {
 	int cost[n][n],kval[n][n],i,j,k,l,cal=0;
 	for(i=1;i<=n;i++)
 	{
 		cost[i][i]=0;
	}
	for(l=2;l<=n;l++)
	{
		for (i=1;i<=n-l+1;i++)
		{
			j=i+l-1;
			cost[i][j]=INT_MAX;
			for(k=i;k<j;k++)
			{
				cal=cost[i][k]+cost[k+1][j]+(dim[i-1]*dim[k]*dim[j]);
				if(cal<cost[i][j])
				{
					cost[i][j]=cal;
				}
			}
		}
	}
	for(int i=1;i<=n;i++)
	{
		for(int j=1;j<=n;j++)
		{

using namespace std;
struct object 
{
	int profit,wt,no;
};
disp(struct object o[],int n)
{
	cout<<"\n";
	for(int i=1;i<=n;i++)
	{
		cout<<endl<<o[i].no<<"\t"<<o[i].profit<<"\t"<<o[i].wt<<"\t";
	}
}
int max(int x,int y)
{
	if(x>=y)
	return x;
	else
	return y;
		
}
int knap(struct object o[],int m,int n)
{
	int table[n+1][m+1],i,w,j;
	for(i=0;i<=n;i++)
	{
		for(w=0;w<=m;w++)
		{
			if(i==0||w==0)
			{
				table[i][w]=0;
			}
			else if(o[i].wt<=w)
			{
				table[i][w]=max(o[i].profit+table[i-1][w-o[i].wt],table[i-1][w]);
			}
			else
			{
				table[i][w]=table[i-1][w];
			}
		}
	}
	cout<<"\nitems included are:\t";
	i=n,j=m;
	while(i>0 && j>0)
	{
		if(table[i][j]!=table[i-1][j])
		{
			cout<<i<<",";
			j=j-o[i].wt;
			i--;
		}
		else
		{
			i--;
		}
	}
	cout<<endl;
	for( i=0;i<=n;i++)
	{
		for( j=0;j<=m;j++)
		{
			cout<<table[i][j];
		}
		cout<<endl;
	}
	return table[n][m];
}
int main()
{
	int n,knapsack,ans;
	struct object o[100];
	cout<<"enter the no of objects";
	cin>>n;
	cout<<"enter the knapsack value";
	cin>>knapsack;
	cout<<"enter the profit and weight";
	for(int i=1;i<=n;i++)
	{
		cin>>o[i].profit;
		cin>>o[i].wt;
		o[i].no=i;
	}
	cout<<"\nobject\tprofit\tweight\tratio";
	disp(o,n);
	cout<<"\nobject\tprofit\tweight\tratio";
	disp(o,n);
	cout<<"\n";
	ans=knap(o,knapsack,n);
	cout<<"\nMAX PROFIT= "<<ans;
	return 0;
}

int LCS(char str1[],char str2[],int m,int n)
{
	int TBL[m+1][n+1],i,j;
	for(i=0;i<=m;i++)
	{
		for(j=0;j<=n;j++)
		{
			if(i==0||j==0)
			{
				TBL[i][j]=0;
			}
			else if(str1[i]==str2[j])
			{
				TBL[i][j]=1+TBL[i-1][j-1];
			}
			else
			{
				TBL[i][j]=max(TBL[i-1][j],TBL[i][j-1]);
			}
		}
	}
	int result;
	result=TBL[m][n];
	int num=result+1;
	cout<<"max length is "<<result;
	char show[result+1];
	i=m,j=n;
	while(i>0 && j>0)
	{
		if(str1[i]=str2[j])
		{
			show[result-1] = str1[i];
            i--;
		    j--;
		    result--;  
		}
		else if (TBL[i-1][j] > TBL[i][j-1]) 
         i--; 
      	else
         j--; 
	}
	 cout << "\nLCS of str1 and str2 is ";
	 for(i=0;i<num;i++)
	 {
	 	cout<<show[i]<<" ";
	  } 
}

void lcs(char str1[],char str2[],int m,int n)
{
	int tab[m+1][n+1],i,j;
	for(int i=0;i<=m;i++)
	{
		for(int j=0;j<=n;j++)
		{
			if(i==0||j==0)
			{
				tab[i][j]=0;
			}
			else if(str1[i-1]==str2[j-1])
			{
				tab[i][j]=1+tab[i-1][j-1];
			}
			else
			{
				tab[i][j]=max(tab[i-1][j],tab[i][j-1]);
			}
		}
	}
	int result;
	result=tab[m][n];
	int num=result+1;
	char show[result+1];
	i=m,j=n;
	while(i>0 && j>0)
	{
		if(str1[i-1]==str2[j-1])
		{
			show[result-1] = str1[i-1];
            i--;
		    j--;
		    result--;  
		}
		else if (tab[i-1][j] > tab[i][j-1]) 
         i--; 
      	else
         j--; 
	}

	{

	} 
}

19/03/2021, 12:41 - Tanisha: Vata, pitta and kapha (the three wrist pulses) are jointly called as Tridosha signals. Tridosha â€“ â€œPulse examination machineâ€ is an automated system to find the diseases and other related information of the human body based on those three pulse readings. The main aim of our project is to design a simple, non-invasive system, painless, cost effective device based on ancient diagnostic technique of Nadi Pariksha (Pulse Detection) to assist ayurvedic practitioners in their routine diagnostic procedures and to measure the health status of the subject using wrist pulse parameters determining the root cause for the same. This project presents the portable prototype of Nadi Pariksha Yantra for pulse reading and analysis.
